<Rate>5< /Rate>< Text>
Upon entering this location it is kind of dark and drab, but you are greeted warmly by the staff.  The ambience is a little bit too dark for my liking. Nonetheless the staff is attentive to your needs and is quick to come take your order. When you place your order it will give you an egg drop soup to go along with your entree and water of course unless you would like an additional or different drink. They offer many types of different drinks fruits and teas. Since I am vegan I did not get the soup so they brought me a house salad the dressing on the salad was delicious to say the least. The fact that they provided me a substitution from their normal side dish accompaniment was a plus for me. I ordered a vegetable udon and the Dr. Pepper as well. They offer many different vegetarian and vegan dishes. the server did not know which were which so he quickly went and found out which I greatly appreciated. As I was enjoying the delicious salad my food arrived nice and hot. Not only was this young man very niceit was not shy to check on me to make sure the food and everything was going well. The pitfall to this location is that is close to UCR so many students flock to this location as they are also open until 2 a.m. making it prime location for students to eat late night. The downfall for most customers is that the students are quite loud and I could hardly hear myself think. They tend to come in flocks so the volume level inside the restaurant without any music or anything playing is way above par to say the least. They do offer a happy hour as well. You can also get food delivered from this location via one of the platform ubereats doordash or GrubHub. Lulu the hostess was extremely nice and always has been when I come here to pick up food. Brian my waiter was exceptional as well. I would highly recommend this place if you can deal with the loud noise from all the patrons that visit.< /Text>

You're not getting the Italian style gourmet spaghetti here. It's bland. Hunts tomato sauce out of a can. Spaghetti was a bit over cooked, but hey, it was an appetizer & cheap (under $5), but we wont be ordering it again. We shared a curry soup based hot pot and ordered beef as our protein. I wish the broth had a stronger curry presence. It was watered down. No coffee of any kind served here (bf was hoping for thai coffee). I ordered an Almond Milk Tea with boba & pudding. Ok this came in a huge glass mug, approx 20oz. (I have one at home!) This was the highlight. I liked it, pudding was more of a jello...hmmm... boba was really good. <sigh> We both said that it is what it is & being so close to UCR i can see the allure. I had hoped to be back to try other menu items, but with some of the reviews... I'm hesitant. So sad, i wanted to like this place. Assessment of the service is pretty spot on. < userid>
104707639892800442091< /userid>
<Text>This is one of my favorite places to go for Mexican food. When I worked nearby, the Special C (2 bean and cheese burritos, chips and salsa, plus a medium drink) was a lifesaver, at only 5 bucks. Their burritos are great and a good size, but what keeps me coming back even when I live half an hour or more away is the shredded beef tacos. I'm not sure what it is, but every time I want tacos, El Burrito Grill's are the ones I crave. Also, the owner's usually there, making sure people like the food and are enjoying their meals. He always seems like he's working as hard as his employees are, which gains a lot of respect from me.
Oh! The chips and salsa are also amazing; for takeout orders they give you an amazing amount (like they don't want any empty space in the bag, even on the cheaper orders), the chips are tostada style, and their salsa is hotter than most other restaurants yet so good I'd rather finish my drink than stop eating it.
Overall, this is where I go whenever I'm in the area, and even still I'll sometimes drive out to Long Beach just to go here.< /Text><Pictures>None<//Pictures><user_name>Sean S</user_name></record>

< Text>
Food is pretty good, prices not so much. There are plenty of great Pho restaurants in the SF/East Bay offering fare of equal quality and far greater quantity. Spent $62 on two clam shells of noodles, half a container of calamari (a $10 container of calamari cleverly packed with wedge of lime INSIDE the box) and three beverages. Not particularly budget friendly -- head up the road to Super Super Pho for great food, relaxed atmosphere and awesome staff.<//Text>

The pan fried noodle came to me as an enormous patty, cut into quarters that were each as big as my hand. With no knife at the table or provided with the meal, I basically set those aside and ignored them. It's probably just as well since they were dripping oil.
The broth and meat were amazingly bland. I could not detect flavors of herbs, meats, spices, or even salt while eating. Considering how amazingly fresh the place smells when you walk in, it's kind of a shock that they could make such lifeless dishes.
The wait staff was friendly enough.

Not going back.<//Text>< Pictures>

<name>Len Welsh</name><response>None</response><UserId.>117508260452840763017</UserId.>< Text>
The people are really friendly and I wanted to like the food, but that was not to be.  I only ordered the pho, but if that is any indication, this restaurant needs to fix its cooking or it will die.  I hope the manager or owner is reading this and will take action.  The pho broth could not in any way be called a beef broth.  It looked more like chicken, though weak even for that.  The flavor was utterly bland, and lacking the traditional pho flavors of burnt onion, burnt ginger, anise, clove, and good fish sauce, not to mention any hint of beef.

It's not that hard to prepare.  Boil beef bones, preferably marrow bones, for a couple of days or in a pressure cooker for half a day, add the ingredients described above except for the fish sauce, cook an hour or two more, get rid of the fat, strain, and you have the broth, ready for fish sauce to be added to get just the right salt balance and the final secret weapon of flavor.  Wild fennel is sprouting up around here all over the place now, and the fresh new greens add wonderful flavor for savvy cooks who want to reap the seasonal rewards nature offers up gratis.

Serve with plenty of fresh basil, cilantro, sliced onion and green onion, and sliced green fresh hot peppers for the heat lovers (traditionally, bean sprouts are served with pho too, but I think they detract from the flavor and so I feed them to my dogs, who are very appreciative).  So easy, really.  Most places around here make nice pho broths (check out, among many others, Phuong Nam, Mekong, and Le Cheval, all in Oakland) but Le Pho needs to learn.<//Text>

<rate>4</rate>< Text>
This place has a good variety of dishes. There are many options for vegetarian diners and also some gluten-free choices!

I ordered a build your own pasta with penne and a garlic pesto sauce. It was pretty good, but I'll request more sauce next time. It reminded me of Olive Garden a bit. I went late in the evening and have a feeling that earlier would have been better/fresher. The breadstick that came with my meal didn't do anything for me, but maybe I'm just picky. It was a bit dry.

The prices seem a little high, but not unreasonable. I expected a larger portion or higher quality for the 14.95 price. There are refills given on the fountain drinks (which include non-sodas like the delightful pink lemonade I had).

Overall not bad, and it's nice to have an Italian place nearby. I do plan on going again earlier in the day and trying the pizza or calzone.< /Text>
